  <raw>Alfa Romeo won't return to USA in 2007; Fiat's sporty brand loses ground in western Europe




Alfa Romeo is postponing a return to the US again. It won't make the move, as originally planned, in 2007, Fiat Group CEO Giuseppe Morchio told Automotive News Europe.
A comeback is part of the Fiat Group's strategy, but a date hasn't been set yet, Morchio said. "We have to fix our operations in Europe before we start thinking about North America."

Alfa Romeo's sales in western Europe are down 5.8 percent. Overall, industry sales in western Europe are down 1.3 percent.
The Fiat Auto subsidiary has sold 138,631 units in the first 10 months of the year, down from 147,120 units during the same period in 2002.
Up in Italy
Alfa's sales are up 2.5 percent in Italy, where it has sold 70,596 units from January through October, but sales of the brand are down in most other European countries. Alfa's biggest decline is in Germany where sales have dropped from 25,700 units in 2001 to 19,000 units last year. Projected sales for 2003 are 15,000 units.
Morchio said one of Herbert Demel's first priorities as new CEO of Fiat Auto is to fix the company's dealer network outside the country.
Production drop
Alfa's production also is down. It will build fewer than 200,000 units for the second year in a row. It hopes to produce more than 200,000 units next year.
Alfa's return to the USA has been plagued by repeated postponements. In March 2000, when Fiat announced its strategic alliance with General Motors, it said Alfa would return to the USA in 2003 with its next-generation Spider.
But the move was postponed to 2004, then to 2005, and, in the summer of 2002, the date was pushed back to 2007. The first two delays resulted from changes to the platform on which the new Spider, code-named project 938, was based. Project 938 was killed in July 2002, when Alfa decided to delay its return until it had a complete range of new vehicles.
The new range, called project 939, includes four cars based on the Premium Vehicle Architecture Alfa developed in cooperation with Saab. The cars are the replacements for the 156 sedan and station wagon and successors to the current Spider and its derived GTV coupe. All will appear in Europe between late 2005 and the middle of 2006.
Alfa wanted these four cars to be ready and in production before re-entering the US market.
It was projecting sales of 50,000-60,000 cars a year in the USA in the medium term.</raw>
